  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_19d10b05-5905-4ccb-8cfb-72a8048790ab'
      });
    }
    
    var initializeSiwa = function() {
      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"

<div id="review_136963769" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/136963769" />
    <a title="Brad" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1022982-brad"><img alt="Brad" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1442484575p2/1022982.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/136963769?book_show_action=true">Dec 28, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Brad" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Brad" href="/user/show/1022982-brad">Brad</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer136963769" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9372196948614724417">I don't know why, but I don't much care to write a review, yet I feel compelled to do so. And because of that you get point form adapted from a discussion I've been having about the comic while reading it. <br/><br/>•One of my favourite parts of <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/107007.The_League_of_Extraordinary_Gentlemen__Vol__2' title='The League of Extraordinary Gentlemen, Vol. 2 by Alan Moore' rel='nofollow noopener'>League of Extraordinary Gentlemen Vol 2</a> are <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/2900017.Kevin_O_Neill' title='Kevin O'Neill' rel='nofollow noopener'>Kevin O'Neill</a>'s pencils. The way he exaggerates features through understatement is difficult to describe, but there is a sort of Victorian reality that he captures that is really effective. Another cool bit of pencilling</span>
  <span id="freeText9372196948614724417" style="display:none">I don't know why, but I don't much care to write a review, yet I feel compelled to do so. And because of that you get point form adapted from a discussion I've been having about the comic while reading it. <br /><br />•One of my favourite parts of <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/107007.The_League_of_Extraordinary_Gentlemen__Vol__2" title="The League of Extraordinary Gentlemen, Vol. 2 by Alan Moore" rel="nofollow noopener">League of Extraordinary Gentlemen Vol 2</a> are <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/2900017.Kevin_O_Neill" title="Kevin O'Neill" rel="nofollow noopener">Kevin O'Neill</a>'s pencils. The way he exaggerates features through understatement is difficult to describe, but there is a sort of Victorian reality that he captures that is really effective. Another cool bit of pencilling is when O'Neill places the League in the background and foregrounds the people of England, fleeing from the cities, getting drunk in alleys, whatever. It creates a sense of the people surrounding <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/3961.Alan_Moore" title="Alan Moore" rel="nofollow noopener">Alan Moore</a>'s anti-heroes, which isn't something you always get in comic books.<br /><br />•There is a cool cameo from Dr. Moreau and all his "Moreauvians" (thanks for the new word, Amber), all of whom live in a forest. The art is bizarre, almost comical, and I had trouble getting into it to begin with. It turned out well though, and I think it really suited the general aesthetic. And there were plenty of extra references to children's lit that I liked. <br /><br />•Big fan of Wilhelmina Harker in the second volume. I see now that Moore is trying to show us a strong woman in a Victorian England which completely frowns on strength in a woman. Quartermain's control begins to slip, and it is banished entirely once Mina takes him to bed. Mina is in control of who she and Quartermain are.<br /><br />•I liked the first sex scene in the Inn, but I didn't care much for the outdoor sex scene that is intruded upon by the Moreauvians. Together they show an interesting shift back and forth between Mina in control and Quartermain trying to regain the control he's lost, and it is nice to see that his attempt to regain control is Moreauvians (I just like hearing that name in my head).<br /><br />SPOILER ALERT (look away)<blockquote>•The rape(s). What to say? I wasn't convinced that Griffin actually raped Mina, although there seems to be some implication of that in her diary response after the Invisible Man's attack, but since the only violation from Griffin we actually see is Mina's severe beating, the question of rape remains up in the air. Interesting, then, that her rape (if that is indeed what it was) is withheld, but we are given a clear view of Hyde raping Griffin for revenge. It is a unsavoury piece typical of Alan Moore’s work, His heroes are nowhere near as heroic as heroes are supposed to be. And even calling them anti-heroes seems too kind. They are villains whom we delude ourselves into thinking are heroic; they’re not heroes.</blockquote>SPOILER OVER<br /><br />•Volume 2 is much better than Volume 1. <br /><br />•I wonder if any of those who died are actually dead. I doubt it. It is a comic book after all, and there was much talk amongst the characters about staged deaths. A little foreshadowing, I've no doubt. <br /><br />•I love Nemo. Mina's my favourite. And Quartermain is my least favourite, but I appreciate the role he plays. And Griffin and Hyde fascinate me.<br /><br />•Avoid this movie at all costs. It is utter crap. Such a shame that it will likely be the last movie Sean Connery ever makes.<br /><br />•The Almanac contains tons of interesting stuff, but it is boring. Seriously boring. Sleep inducing, in fact. <br /><br />That’s it for my lazy list. Hope you enjoyed it. </span>
  <a data-text-id="9372196948614724417" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

However, Alan Moore's seeming obsession with creating ancilliary documents as companion pieces to his stories is getting a bit tiresome.<br/><br/><i>The New Traveller's Almanac</i> included with volume two is insufferably long and tedious prose. Moore melds all manner of details from sundry novels into one universe in the context of a travelogue of weird phenomena (perhaps channeling Charles Fort if Fort had a PhD in Victorian literature), but it quickly loses all redeeming val</span>
  <span id="freeText14391570910073118919" style="display:none">Even better story than volume one. However, Alan Moore's seeming obsession with creating ancilliary documents as companion pieces to his stories is getting a bit tiresome.<br /><br /><i>The New Traveller's Almanac</i> included with volume two is insufferably long and tedious prose. Moore melds all manner of details from sundry novels into one universe in the context of a travelogue of weird phenomena (perhaps channeling Charles Fort if Fort had a PhD in Victorian literature), but it quickly loses all redeeming value when it stops being a humorous novelty.<br /><br />This is a shame because the graphic portion of this book is damn near perfect, but the <i>Almanac</i> takes up almost a quarter of the book for no good reason that could have been much better spent on the actual freaking plot.</span>

  <span id="freeText5091160639542612138" style="display:none">This is one of those situations where there was just more stuff I disliked than stuff I liked. <div id="review_2881553056" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2881553056" />
    <a title="J" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1162892-j"><img alt="J" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1300246430p2/1162892.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2881553056?book_show_action=true">Jul 08, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="J" class="user" itemprop="url" name="J" href="/user/show/1162892-j">J</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1162892-j?shelf=comics">comics</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2881553056" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6240781882238445193">Whew, the travelogue at the end was rather tedious even if it did have some interesting bits to it. One of the weaknesses of late-Moore is his tendency to over-written expansive prose. The clean poetry of his earlier years has given away to long-windedness. The illustrated comic parts were fun and the plotting is enjoyable and the art is a treat. I'd trade all the end papers nonsense for six more pages of illustrated adventure where Moore's word count is more curtailed.</span>

          </span>
        </div>

    <a title="Shannon Appelcline" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/10160415-shannon-appelcline"><img alt="Shannon Appelcline" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1339479517p2/10160415.jpg" /></a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Shannon Appelcline" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Shannon Appelcline" href="/user/show/10160415-shannon-appelcline">Shannon Appelcline</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10160415-shannon-appelcline?shelf=comics-indy">comics-indy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10160415-shannon-appelcline?shelf=comics">comics</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3014337604" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12833516627450415221"><b>League Vol. 2.</b> Moore casts his nets wider in this second volume by incorporating the tales of H.G. Wells, primarily <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/8909.The_War_of_the_Worlds' title='The War of the Worlds by H.G. Wells' rel='nofollow noopener'>The War of the Worlds</a>, but with an amusing diversion to <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/29981.The_Island_of_Doctor_Moreau' title='The Island of Doctor Moreau by H.G. Wells' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Island of Doctor Moreau</a>. The result is a very different sort of adventure tale from the first, but one that's both more evocative and engaging. (And that's not even counting the wonderful first issue, which mashes together a few Martian planetary romances.)<br/><br/>Meanwhile, Moore dramatically develops the pulp heroes that we met </span>
  <span id="freeText12833516627450415221" style="display:none"><b>League Vol. 2.</b> Moore casts his nets wider in this second volume by incorporating the tales of H.G. Wells, primarily <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/8909.The_War_of_the_Worlds" title="The War of the Worlds by H.G. Wells" rel="nofollow noopener">The War of the Worlds</a>, but with an amusing diversion to <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/29981.The_Island_of_Doctor_Moreau" title="The Island of Doctor Moreau by H.G. Wells" rel="nofollow noopener">The Island of Doctor Moreau</a>. The result is a very different sort of adventure tale from the first, but one that's both more evocative and engaging. (And that's not even counting the wonderful first issue, which mashes together a few Martian planetary romances.)<br /><br />Meanwhile, Moore dramatically develops the pulp heroes that we met in the first volume, turning them into true characters with character arcs all their own. It's wonderful to see how they all change (after the foundation of their characters in V1).<br /><br />Is this volume a bit too violent and explicit? Perhaps. It's certainly part of the deconstruction that Moore began in V1, but it may go too far for the faint of heart [4+/5].</span>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_8740367" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/8740367" />
    <a title="Rob" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/199290-rob"><img alt="Rob" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1184889068p2/199290.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/8740367?book_show_action=true">Nov 06, 2007</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Rob" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Rob" href="/user/show/199290-rob">Rob</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">SF and comic geeks</span></div>

        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer8740367" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13355494402430574868">In my opinion, this is a hell of a good read.<br/><br/>The author took famous characters from Victorian popular literature and put them together into a 'special action group' that works for MI5 in the last decade of 19th Century England. MI5 is lead by Mycroft Holmes by the way.<br/><br/>The League consists of Mina Murray, Alan Quartermain, Henry Jekyll and his alter-ego, Captain Nemo and Hawley Griffin, otherwise known as the Invisible Man.<br/><br/>And the situation they have to deal with is the invasion of Earth by Mars.<br/><br/>I</span>
  <span id="freeText13355494402430574868" style="display:none">In my opinion, this is a hell of a good read.<br /><br />The author took famous characters from Victorian popular literature and put them together into a 'special action group' that works for MI5 in the last decade of 19th Century England. MI5 is lead by Mycroft Holmes by the way.<br /><br />The League consists of Mina Murray, Alan Quartermain, Henry Jekyll and his alter-ego, Captain Nemo and Hawley Griffin, otherwise known as the Invisible Man.<br /><br />And the situation they have to deal with is the invasion of Earth by Mars.<br /><br />I've read it many times. the artwork is excellent. Every frame just reeks of Victorian. If you look you can find a website that deconstructs this book frame by frame. And it's amazing how much the artist jammed into his work.<br /><br />The story is excellent, much more human than most of these 'grand adventures' are. None of the characters breaks character, and I got to like all of them, for the most part.<br /><br />I'd recommend this book for a pleasant, amusing and very different read.</span>
  <a data-text-id="13355494402430574868" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer191099865" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5832959217326611596">So Alan Moore hates women. I guess having read V for Vendetta and Watchmen should have made me aware of that, but call me slow.<br/>While the story and art were as interesting as in the first book, the details were mostly gross. First of all, two whole sex scenes between Mina and Allan, which I could have tolerated if not for the mutual professions of love. Then there is an assault on Mina where she doesn't vamp out and fight back. Lastly, someone is raped to death. Oh yeah, and Martians are invading</span>
  <span id="freeText5832959217326611596" style="display:none">So Alan Moore hates women. I guess having read V for Vendetta and Watchmen should have made me aware of that, but call me slow.<br />While the story and art were as interesting as in the first book, the details were mostly gross. First of all, two whole sex scenes between Mina and Allan, which I could have tolerated if not for the mutual professions of love. Then there is an assault on Mina where she doesn't vamp out and fight back. Lastly, someone is raped to death. Oh yeah, and Martians are invading.<br />The most interesting character turned out the be Hyde. I wish we could have seen more of him. Nemo, for all that is was his ship, was barely there. I guess the story relies on previous knowledge of these characters, but this does not excuse lack of development.</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer7668309367497012738">Volume one of this graphic novel left me on the fence. I wasn’t overly interested in carrying on, yet because my friend had let me borrow her omnibus I decided it couldn’t hurt. After all, it was something that could be completed in no time at all.<br/><br/>Truthfully, I enjoy volume two much more than I enjoyed volume one. There was more substance to it than the first book, with more happening throughout. We truly see our characters, watching them interact with each other, seeing the way they deal with a</span>
  <span id="freeText7668309367497012738" style="display:none">Volume one of this graphic novel left me on the fence. I wasn’t overly interested in carrying on, yet because my friend had let me borrow her omnibus I decided it couldn’t hurt. After all, it was something that could be completed in no time at all.<br /><br />Truthfully, I enjoy volume two much more than I enjoyed volume one. There was more substance to it than the first book, with more happening throughout. We truly see our characters, watching them interact with each other, seeing the way they deal with a catastrophic event. Whilst I wouldn’t say it was full of twists and turns, it did provide more than just a straight fact-telling story.<br /><br />Overall, much more enjoyable than the first volume.</span>

<div id="review_3065820873" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3065820873" />
    <a title="Charles" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1336573-charles"><img alt="Charles" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1442468643p2/1336573.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3065820873?book_show_action=true">Nov 29, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Charles" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Charles" href="/user/show/1336573-charles">Charles</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1336573-charles?shelf=graphic-novels">graphic-novels</a>
          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3065820873" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10397965943757820625">A mixed bag. The graphic novel part of this was much superior to that in Volume 1. It started on Mars, featuring a John Carter stand in and the Tharks fighting with some mollusk type beings who then fled in rocket ships to earth, and this turned out to be the War of the Worlds Invasion. The opening was interesting and sparked my imagination but it was irritating that much of the early dialogue was rendered in "Martian," meaning symbols that couldn't be read. Once the invasion of earth began, the</span>
  <span id="freeText10397965943757820625" style="display:none">A mixed bag. The graphic novel part of this was much superior to that in Volume 1. It started on Mars, featuring a John Carter stand in and the Tharks fighting with some mollusk type beings who then fled in rocket ships to earth, and this turned out to be the War of the Worlds Invasion. The opening was interesting and sparked my imagination but it was irritating that much of the early dialogue was rendered in "Martian," meaning symbols that couldn't be read. Once the invasion of earth began, there was quite a lot excitement as the League of Extraordinary Gentlemen were tested to their limits. I certainly liked this part well enough that I might even have given it 4 stars. However, the book ended with a very lengthy travelogue that basically threw out imaginary names and lands as if they existed in reality and made an effort to connect them into a kind of coherent story. The problem with this part was that there was just too much of it, with no descriptions or real details. It read like an exercise in name dropping and it was extremely boring to me to the point that I finally began to just scan it. This took away a star. </span>
  <a data-text-id="10397965943757820625" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_937113689" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/937113689" />
    <a title="Brittany" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/16871066-brittany"><img alt="Brittany" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1475420292p2/16871066.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/937113689?book_show_action=true">May 14, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Brittany" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Brittany" href="/user/show/16871066-brittany">Brittany</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16871066-brittany?shelf=reviewed">reviewed</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer937113689" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1923791845911919707">I really was not expecting much after volume 1, but I already had it at home so I wondered if it might improve.<br/><br/>I was wrong. There are brief neat moments. My favorite takes place when Nemo comments that he is prepared to destroy a bridge full of civilians to trap the aliens and protect the greater good, and Hyde taunts him into saying that it's no great strategic loss if he must do so, anyway. Nemo says, "Besides, they're only-" and Hyde says, "Human?" And Nemo finishes, "English". Nemo is the su</span>
  <span id="freeText1923791845911919707" style="display:none">I really was not expecting much after volume 1, but I already had it at home so I wondered if it might improve.<br /><br />I was wrong. There are brief neat moments. My favorite takes place when Nemo comments that he is prepared to destroy a bridge full of civilians to trap the aliens and protect the greater good, and Hyde taunts him into saying that it's no great strategic loss if he must do so, anyway. Nemo says, "Besides, they're only-" and Hyde says, "Human?" And Nemo finishes, "English". Nemo is the subject of various racist slurs throughout both novels and this was a good moment of him responding back to that without a damn. Yeah, they hate him. He hates them right back, although he still willingly protects them at various points because he's a better person in many ways. I also liked that there were moments of teamwork and at least Nemo, Allan and Hyde care about Mina's well-being by this novel.<br /><br />Mina loses what little control she had over the group in the novel. Sure, she can still lead Allan around, especially since he's head over heels for her, and she still fascinates Hyde, but no one else respects her and she serves more as a spectator and messenger than anything else here. Her 'romance' with Allan was one of the dumbest I've seen in a while. The only redeeming quality was how Allan reassured her over her scars. Her parting with Hyde is creepy, at best. "May I touch your breast?" Well at least it's a straightforward last request.<br /><br />There's a bad place reserved in the afterlife for rapists and attempted rapists. There's a worse place for people who think rape is a proper form of revenge, especially for rape. I don't know if Moore wants us to sympathize with the Invisible Man (and I don't) or cheer Hyde's butt-raping and otherwise torturing him to death in revenge for Mina, or just feel conflicted on who should receive worse punishment. But like Nemo said, Hyde teaches terror. He's there for nothing else.<br /><br />Nemo was again the most interesting character, even more so than Mina. I wish we had more of his story.<br /><br />The art is still pretty awful. Mina is treated like crap. Tons and tons of men doing stuff and the one woman is a weak little flower. There's animal cruelty and aliens invade London and somehow Moore made me not even care. I don't question what makes a hero after reading this. I question what Moore wanted: did someone want him to make a heroic group of these people and Moore then went about demonstrating just how STUPID an idea that is or did he want to see if he could sell this group of unlikeable people as heroes, like Stan Lee did with Tony Stark? Whatever the case, again: if you romanticize Victorian lit, read this and bring yourself back to reality. If you don't, watch the film. It's still shockingly better.</span>
  <a data-text-id="1923791845911919707" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_145798451" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/145798451" />
    <a title="William Thomas" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1143572-william-thomas"><img alt="William Thomas" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1286686020p2/1143572.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/145798451?book_show_action=true">Feb 03, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="William Thomas" class="user" itemprop="url" name="William Thomas" href="/user/show/1143572-william-thomas">William Thomas</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1143572-william-thomas?shelf=horror">horror</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1143572-william-thomas?shelf=modern-art">modern-art</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1143572-william-thomas?shelf=science-fiction">science-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1143572-william-thomas?shelf=graphic-novel">graphic-novel</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1143572-william-thomas?shelf=post-watchmen-comic-books">post-watchmen-comic-books</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1143572-william-thomas?shelf=believe-the-hype">believe-the-hype</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1143572-william-thomas?shelf=modern-literature">modern-literature</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer145798451" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17923443999498146313">When I was sixteen, I was at a comic book convention in Chicago, waiting in line for the guest of honor's autograph- Frank Miller. Alongside him were others like garth Ennis and Alex Ross who were doing signings as well. For some reason or other they brought up Alan Moore and joked about how he was most likely sitting in a closet with a candle and a typewriter in a castle somewhere in England. Having only seen one picture of Moore at the time, used over and over again for all of his works and in</span>
  <span id="freeText17923443999498146313" style="display:none">When I was sixteen, I was at a comic book convention in Chicago, waiting in line for the guest of honor's autograph- Frank Miller. Alongside him were others like garth Ennis and Alex Ross who were doing signings as well. For some reason or other they brought up Alan Moore and joked about how he was most likely sitting in a closet with a candle and a typewriter in a castle somewhere in England. Having only seen one picture of Moore at the time, used over and over again for all of his works and interviews, I thought this was completely plausible. I still do. <br /><br />I hear hear he is studying chaos magick now. A strange man, he is. But a brilliant one on the whole.<br /><br />Alan Moore is a victim. His work has been bastardized by Hollywood on more than one occasion. His art has been brutalized and raped and been turned into the typical horse shit that you see when you see V for Vendetta and the movie adaptation of The League of Extraordinary Gentlemen. And none of these movies can do his work any sort or form of justice because they do not express the very literary quality of the books but instead focus on the novel idea of it all and sensationalize the aesthetic, the surface tones, instead of the deeper meanings and the art of it all. So if you have only seen the Gentlemen movie, please read these books. These two volumes at least. Because they are a large part of the reason we can call comic books a legitimate art form.<br /><br />So here in this volume, Alan Moore takes us a little farther out there than the previous volume. He takes us to Mars. He shows us Gullivar. And then he brings us back to earth to rewrite War of the Worlds. And he does it in a way that makes it look effortless, literary and brilliant. <br /><br />The main focus of this book, the way I saw it, was on Mr. Hyde. I loved seeing his character become a focal point here, and I loved all of the humanizing aspects as well as the polarizing ones in his offhand racism and his casual violence. But most of all I loved his sense of duty and justice and his unrequited love and how twisted it all became in his hands. <br /><br />The most disturbing part of the book was probably Quartermaine sexing it up with Mina Harker. Because all I could then picture was Sean Connery having sex with a cartoon. And it frightened me.<br /><br />As for the artwork, it is not typically something I would enjoy but for this book seemed a perfect fit. O'Neill ha a way of making the inks look both frantic and sharp and I can't be sure but it looks like he works with a barely skeletal pencil layout before he dives in with the inks. Which may add to the urgency of some of his lines.<br /><br />The final verdict? Pitch-perfect.</span>
  <a data-text-id="17923443999498146313" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_379627761" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/379627761" />
    <a title="Zedsdead" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/8224038-zedsdead"><img alt="Zedsdead" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1332172185p2/8224038.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/379627761?book_show_action=true">Jul 29, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer379627761" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5254577753578083980">The War of the Worlds comes to London and it's up to the League to prevent the downfall of England...and perhaps mankind.<br/><br/>The first issue, set entirely on Mars, strikes me as a fail. It's largely dialogue free (well, the dialogue is written in what is presumably Martian) and the Martian battle illustrations are chaotically uninformative. Who's fighting whom? How many factions even are there? Why do some of them blast off and attack Earth? This is some poor storytelling.<br/><br/>Issue 2 gets back to busine</span>
  <span id="freeText5254577753578083980" style="display:none">The War of the Worlds comes to London and it's up to the League to prevent the downfall of England...and perhaps mankind.<br /><br />The first issue, set entirely on Mars, strikes me as a fail. It's largely dialogue free (well, the dialogue is written in what is presumably Martian) and the Martian battle illustrations are chaotically uninformative. Who's fighting whom? How many factions even are there? Why do some of them blast off and attack Earth? This is some poor storytelling.<br /><br />Issue 2 gets back to business and captures that old-timey alien invasion flavor. In fact the rest of the book is pretty much rocket sauce. As in v1, the plot wanders all over the place--a natural result of the title's determination to visit every work of classic literature out there--but it's filled with moments that are so cruel, appalling, and organic that they come to life in a way comics don't often achieve. <br /><br />This volume makes me feel filthy, and I can't tell if it's because of or in spite of that that I appreciate it so much.<br /><br />Plot points:<br /><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[<br />--An entire issue is dedicated to muddled Martian battle sequences, until a few spaceships blast off.<br />--Hyde casually ponders to Mina why he doesn't simply rape and behead her. He politely, distractedly requests that she leave his presence before he breaks her jaw.<br />--A cylinder crashes in London. A laser tentacle burns everyone in the neighborhood. The League is sent to investigate.<br />--Hawley Griffin sneaks off and makes a deal with the Martians, providing intelligence in exchange for a position of power in post-human Earth. While stealing British military plans, he beats Mina half to death.<br />--Mina and Quatermain are sent to fetch a crate from Dr. Moreau. They begin a sexual relationship and we finally see under her scarf. No, that's not an entendre.<br />--Nemo battles the invaders from the Thames until they trap the Nautilus with alien vegetation.<br />--Hyde tracks Griffin to their base and takes his time torturing, raping, and mutilating him for betraying the team and harming Mina. As he dines with Nemo, blood gradually becomes visible all over Hyde and...well pretty much everything in the room, indicating that the invisible man had finally succumbed to his injuries.<br />--At the London Bridge, Hyde sacrifices himself to delay the massed invaders until Moreau's secret weapon can be deployed. It's a hybrid bacterium and the Martians are defeated.<br />--Incensed that their employers used the League to enact biological warfare, Nemo quits the team and departs.<br />--Mina joins a commune and leaves a despondent Quatermain alone on a bench in soon-to-be-renamed-Hyde Park. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span></span>
  <a data-text-id="5254577753578083980" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer10561461633620465167">Wow. Uhm. Yeah, so what to say here. This is one of those things that I sort of loved but will never, ever recommend to anyone. Ever. Moreso even than Game of Thrones. I actually really liked it, but... wow. It had these great bits in it where Hyde only listens to Mina, and they have this lovely moment, and I was like AWWWW. And even the part where Griffin attacks Mina was so heartbreaking and awful but wonderful because you knew Hyde was going to come back and save her. But then when Hyde did e</span>
  <span id="freeText10561461633620465167" style="display:none">Wow. Uhm. Yeah, so what to say here. This is one of those things that I sort of loved but will never, ever recommend to anyone. Ever. Moreso even than Game of Thrones. I actually really liked it, but... wow. It had these great bits in it where Hyde only listens to Mina, and they have this lovely moment, and I was like AWWWW. And even the part where Griffin attacks Mina was so heartbreaking and awful but wonderful because you knew Hyde was going to come back and save her. But then when Hyde did exact his revenge, I was like "yup, didn't see that coming." Guys...he raped Griffin to death and then threatened to kill Nemo and the other guy if they told Mina. I was like...<br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380392301i/755271.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>And then he lied about it to Mina so she wouldn't be upset! And the worst part of it all was I caught myself thinking "Griffin had it coming, he raped all those girls at the school, and he terrorized Mina." This book is bad for your soul. If you see this book your response should be:<br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380392301ra/755272.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>There was so much cartoon nudity it wasn't even funny! They had sex in the woods!<br>And then there wass Nemo running around declaring his outrage at everything, and NO ONE LISTENED! <br>And then there was Dr. Moreau with his hoards of hybrids:<br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380392301ra/755273.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>Moore managed to dredge up the most immoral and terrible people in the history of English literature (seriously, these people make Nemo look like the chaplain at your local parish), put them all together, and added some aliens for fun. It ends how you imagine it would. It's awful.<br><br>And yet... there are these wonderful bits. There are moments of light. And even though they are quickly smothered by either sex or blood, there are moments of truth. Are they enough to redeem the comic? I don't know. Maybe not. Probably not, actually. <br>So in closing, I liked it but don't read it.</span>

<div id="review_39639827" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">

    <a title="Ma&#39;Belle" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1663826-ma-belle"><img alt="Ma&#39;Belle" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1440555221p2/1663826.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/39639827?book_show_action=true">Dec 08, 2008</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Ma&#39;Belle" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Ma&#39;Belle" href="/user/show/1663826-ma-belle">Ma&#39;Belle</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1663826-ma-belle?shelf=comics-graphic-novels">comics-graphic-novels</a>
          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer39639827" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7714302136871525656">Reviewing any of the three volumes in Alan Moore's League of Extraordinary Gentlemen series is a difficult task. Without reading the edited annotations of Jess Nevins, the story seems somewhat shallow and bland. However, the annotations of various librarians and connoisseurs of Victorian-era literature add so much insight into almost every panel that it can become overwhelming and the story itself can get lost in the backdrop.<br/><br/>Another reviewer on goodreads has said half of the genius in LoEG is i</span>
  <span id="freeText7714302136871525656" style="display:none">Reviewing any of the three volumes in Alan Moore's League of Extraordinary Gentlemen series is a difficult task. Without reading the edited annotations of Jess Nevins, the story seems somewhat shallow and bland. However, the annotations of various librarians and connoisseurs of Victorian-era literature add so much insight into almost every panel that it can become overwhelming and the story itself can get lost in the backdrop.<br /><br />Another reviewer on goodreads has said half of the genius in LoEG is in its often obscure literary references. I'd go so far as to say this accounts for at least 75% of its greatness. For this reason, it's hard for me to recommend the series to anyone who lacks the motivation and patience to read the annotations as well (which can also be found for free online), but easy to attribute a great amount of respect to Moore for this massive undertaking. It proves, more than anything else about the author, his ability to do exhaustive research and then adapt it to the comic book medium.</span>
  <a data-text-id="7714302136871525656" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Simon" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Simon" href="/user/show/745423-simon">Simon</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/745423-simon?shelf=sf-fantasy">sf-fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/745423-simon?shelf=comics">comics</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
                  <em>
                    This review has been hidden because it contains spoilers. To view it,
                    <a href="#" onclick="Effect.toggle(&#39;reviewTextContainer13484999&#39;); return false;">click here.</a>
                  </em>
              <span id="reviewTextContainer13484999" class="readable"
                    style="display:none"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13325064330517441598">Quite a disappointment after the richness, complexity and wit of volume one. A stunning opening chapter whets the appetite, but thereafter the plot meanders in several directions at once, none of them satisfying. The members of the league (and writer Moore) seem more interested in internal frictions within the group than the threat they are facing. O'Neill's artwork is as accomplished as ever, and Jekyll has an interesting scene, but Nemo is given nothing whatsoever to do, and the "clever" refer</span>
  <span id="freeText13325064330517441598" style="display:none">Quite a disappointment after the richness, complexity and wit of volume one. A stunning opening chapter whets the appetite, but thereafter the plot meanders in several directions at once, none of them satisfying. The members of the league (and writer Moore) seem more interested in internal frictions within the group than the threat they are facing. O'Neill's artwork is as accomplished as ever, and Jekyll has an interesting scene, but Nemo is given nothing whatsoever to do, and the "clever" references to other famous literary characters seem perfunctory and pointless.<br />At the end Moore splits the group up as if wishing to put an end to the series. I think he made the right choice. You're better off re-reading volume one instead.</span>
  <a data-text-id="13325064330517441598" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">Alan Moore</span></div>

        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
                  <em>
                    This review has been hidden because it contains spoilers. To view it,
                    <a href="#" onclick="Effect.toggle(&#39;reviewTextContainer29948660&#39;); return false;">click here.</a>

              <span id="reviewTextContainer29948660" class="readable"
                    style="display:none"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7049068376120802080">The premise behind these stories seems like genius. Put together a cast of Victorian all stars and have them do extraordinary things. Instead, vol. 2 has little action in terms of a team doing anything. The "love" story is pathetic. The nudity and sex scenes are stuff for immature readers....there is no sensuality or even eroticism, it just feels like "Hey look I can put a nude woman in this graphic novel and then I can have this guy have sex with her...he he he I am so cool." <br/>This one also suff</span>
  <span id="freeText7049068376120802080" style="display:none">The premise behind these stories seems like genius. Put together a cast of Victorian all stars and have them do extraordinary things. Instead, vol. 2 has little action in terms of a team doing anything. The "love" story is pathetic. The nudity and sex scenes are stuff for immature readers....there is no sensuality or even eroticism, it just feels like "Hey look I can put a nude woman in this graphic novel and then I can have this guy have sex with her...he he he I am so cool." <br />This one also suffers from Deus Ex Machina big time. Which I realize Moore is borrowing from H.G. Wells, but still.<br /><br />Read this book, because you should read everything you can and make your own opinions.</span>

    <a title="Jakob" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3303892-jakob"><img alt="Jakob" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1401451447p2/3303892.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/90338272?book_show_action=true">Feb 18, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jakob" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jakob" href="/user/show/3303892-jakob">Jakob</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3303892-jakob?shelf=graphic-novel">graphic-novel</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer90338272" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14747111742207490046">I don't really know what it was that compelled me to finish reading this book but when it was over all I was left with was a sick feeling in my stomach. Having read some of Alan Moore's previous work and enjoyed it somewhat I thought this might make for an entertaining read. Unfortunately this was not the case. It did however give me a much clearer view of Moore's past works. What I had mistaken in the past as bitter social commentary was now revealed for what it was, misanthropic bile which had</span>
  <span id="freeText14747111742207490046" style="display:none">I don't really know what it was that compelled me to finish reading this book but when it was over all I was left with was a sick feeling in my stomach. Having read some of Alan Moore's previous work and enjoyed it somewhat I thought this might make for an entertaining read. Unfortunately this was not the case. It did however give me a much clearer view of Moore's past works. What I had mistaken in the past as bitter social commentary was now revealed for what it was, misanthropic bile which had finally reached it's ugly culmination in this pathetic and vile work of fiction.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="14747111742207490046" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

              <span id="reviewTextContainer64501144" class="readable"

<span id="freeTextContainer4556092149124608103">I was hoping that, as with some of the other graphic novels I've read, <i>The League of Extraordinary Gentlemen</i> would get better as it went on. <br/><br/>I was sorely disappointed. The mashing up of different classic novels felt forced, there was little character development, and, to be perfectl honest, I found some of the content disturbing and repellent. I'm not really into rape. At all, actually. </span>

          </span>
        </div>

Rather than the garish action flick, the comic is almost satirical and definitely cynical. While perhaps not the most exciting a heroic piece you'll ever read there is something compelling about the flawed heroes and their escapades.</span>

          </span>

        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2840148184?book_show_action=true">May 30, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Paul Weiss" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Paul Weiss" href="/user/show/51664350-paul-weiss">Paul Weiss</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/51664350-paul-weiss?shelf=graphic-novel">graphic-novel</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2840148184" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16551876401958547458"><b>Alan Moore and Kevin O'Neill continue to pay tribute to Victorian adventure classics!</b><br/><br/><b>THE LEAGUE OF EXTRAORDINARY GENTLEMEN, VOL 2</b>, like its stellar predecessor, is a graphic novel and is most assuredly not a comic book intended for children. Rather it is solid proof that mainstream comic books can be combined with exciting, imaginative adventure and story-telling, illustrated with serious, skilled artwork that merits close examination in each and every panel aimed at serious adult readers with e</span>
  <span id="freeText16551876401958547458" style="display:none"><b>Alan Moore and Kevin O'Neill continue to pay tribute to Victorian adventure classics!</b><br /><br /><b>THE LEAGUE OF EXTRAORDINARY GENTLEMEN, VOL 2</b>, like its stellar predecessor, is a graphic novel and is most assuredly not a comic book intended for children. Rather it is solid proof that mainstream comic books can be combined with exciting, imaginative adventure and story-telling, illustrated with serious, skilled artwork that merits close examination in each and every panel aimed at serious adult readers with eclectic tastes in classic literature. <b>THE LEAGUE OF EXTRAORDINARY GENTLEMEN, VOL 2</b> is at once a pastiche and a tribute to the skills of an extraordinary, lengthy and almost bewildering list of adventure, mystery and horror writers of the late eighteenth and early nineteenth centuries.<br /><br />Moore's eclectic team of stalwart adventurers - Mina Harker of Bram Stoker's <b>DRACULA</b> fame; Edward Hyde, the brutal alter ego of Robert Louis Stevenson's gentler Dr Jekyll; H Merle Haggard's aging Allan Quartermain, the basis of modern Hollywood's <b>INDIANA JONES</b>; HG Wells' Hawley Griffin, better known as <b>THE INVISIBLE MAN</b>; and, finally, Captain Nemo, Jules Vernes' inscrutable captain of the fabulous Nautilus - defend the earth against an invasion from Mars.<br /><br />Moore's borrowed cast of characters leaps off the page and into life under the skilled artistry of Kevin O'Neill. But alert readers will quickly discover that it doesn't end with this short list of main players and will delight in scavenging for even the most fleeting references to an almost endless list of literary luminaries - John Carter of Edgar Rice Burroughs' Mars series; his likely inspiration, Lieutenant Gullivar Jones; Alphonse Moreau; Rupert the Bear (honest!); Badger and Toad from <b>THE WIND IN THE WILLOWS</b>; Ishmael; Fu Manchu ... the list just goes on and on!<br /><br />Be advised. Readers who consider themselves to be faint of heart should know that Kevin O'Neill has given himself full permission to display violence, fighting, bloodletting, death (and did I mention sex?) in the most graphic fashion. But this is far from a criticism, it is only a caution in the full understanding that some potential readers will simply not enjoy the degree to which O'Neill has visually let loose the free flow of blood, guts and unbridled sexuality. Thankfully, I am not on that list and can say that I enjoyed every single word and every single illustration immensely. I'm only sorry to realize that there are only two volumes left in the series which I will be purchasing just as soon as I finish this review.<br /><br />Paul Weiss</span>
  <a data-text-id="16551876401958547458" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_2637613770" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2637613770" />
    <a title="Sud666" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/36890366-sud666"><img alt="Sud666" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1418437112p2/36890366.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2637613770?book_show_action=true">Aug 15, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Sud666" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Sud666" href="/user/show/36890366-sud666">Sud666</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/36890366-sud666?shelf=sci-fi">sci-fi</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/36890366-sud666?shelf=comics">comics</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2637613770" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4594679089076206846">Alan Moore's excellent League of Extraordinary Gentlemen continues in this second volume. Moore channels his inner H.G. Wells in this volume drawing deep influences from "War of the Worlds" and "The Island of Dr. Moreau".<br/><br/>The League is forced to help Mycroft Holmes and the British government deal with an Alien invasion from Mars. This story has a little bit of everything from Martian invaders, the conflict between the invaders and normal humans, and an interesting cast of characters. The Mina Har</span>
  <span id="freeText4594679089076206846" style="display:none">Alan Moore's excellent League of Extraordinary Gentlemen continues in this second volume. Moore channels his inner H.G. Wells in this volume drawing deep influences from "War of the Worlds" and "The Island of Dr. Moreau".<br /><br />The League is forced to help Mycroft Holmes and the British government deal with an Alien invasion from Mars. This story has a little bit of everything from Martian invaders, the conflict between the invaders and normal humans, and an interesting cast of characters. The Mina Harker/Mr. Hyde/Alan Quartermain confluence of emotions makes a huge return in this issue. While Alan's relationship with Mina makes sense, it is Mr. Hyde's fascinating response to her that is interesting. No spoilers, but the Invisible Man will certainly regret his actions.<br />I also enjoyed the strange look at Dr. Moreau and his hybrid solution to the invasion is excellent. Kevin Oniell's artwork, while not usually to my stylistic preference, seems to work for this story. The Victorian setting melds well with the artistic style and I rather appreciated it.<br /><br />Each of the six main issues combines into this volume. As with the first volume, after each story, there is a written addendum that details the world of the LOEG and the League itself. These are told in a newspaper pulp style and is rather interesting. It gives a hint as to the vast imagination that is Alan Moore.<br /><br />Highly recommended for anyone who appreciates a "different" type of super-hero group. Alan Moore's League is a great read and something very different from the usual comics.</span>
  <a data-text-id="4594679089076206846" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!

      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name

      }
    }
    else {

    }

    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

      <div id="aboutAuthor" class=" clearFloats bigBox"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground"><a href="/author/show/3961.Alan_Moore">About Alan Moore</a></h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent">
          <div class='bookAuthorProfile'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__topContainer'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__photoContainer'>
<a href="/author/show/3961.Alan_Moore"><div class='bookAuthorProfile__photo' style='background-image: url(https://images.gr-assets.com/authors/1304944713p3/3961.jpg);'></div>
</a></div>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__widgetContainer'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__name'>
<a href="/author/show/3961.Alan_Moore">Alan Moore
</a></div>
<div class='goodreadsAuthorBadge'></div>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__followerCount'>
16,139
followers
</div>

</div>
</div>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer1845794325806649677">Alan Moore is an English writer most famous for his influential work in comics, including the acclaimed graphic novels <i>Watchmen, V for Vendetta</i> and <i>From Hell</i>. He has also written a novel, <i>Voice of the Fire</i>, and performs "workings" (one-off performance art/spoken word pieces) with The Moon and Serpent Grand Egyptian Theatre of Marvels, some of which have been released on CD.<br/><br/>As a comics writer, Moor</span>
  <span id="freeText1845794325806649677" style="display:none">Alan Moore is an English writer most famous for his influential work in comics, including the acclaimed graphic novels <i>Watchmen, V for Vendetta</i> and <i>From Hell</i>. He has also written a novel, <i>Voice of the Fire</i>, and performs "workings" (one-off performance art/spoken word pieces) with The Moon and Serpent Grand Egyptian Theatre of Marvels, some of which have been released on CD.<br /><br />As a comics writer, Moore is notable for being one of the first writers to apply literary and formalist sensibilities to the mainstream of the medium. As well as including challenging subject matter and adult themes, he brings a wide range of influences to his work, from the literary–authors such as William S. Burroughs, Thomas Pynchon, Robert Anton Wilson and Iain Sinclair; New Wave science fiction writers such as Michael Moorcock; horror writers such as Clive Barker; to the cinematic–filmmakers such as Nicolas Roeg. Influences within comics include Will Eisner, Harvey Kurtzman, Jack Kirby and Bryan Talbot.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="1845794325806649677" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

</div>
</div>

With a cast-list that includes many of the most iconic figures from literature and pop culture, and a tempo that conveys the terrible momentum of inevitable events, this is literally and literarily the story to end all stories. Originally published as a six-issue run of unfashionable, outmoded and flimsy children\'s comics that would make you appear emotionally backward if you read them on the bus, this climactic magnum opus also reprints classic English super-team publication The Seven Stars from the murky black-and-white reaches of 1964. A magnificent celebration of everything comics were, are and could be, any appreciator or student of the medium would be unwise to miss The League of Extraordinary Gentlemen, Volume IV: THE
